Gu Yingfen Passed Through Shanghai Yesterday

No Definite News on Huang Shaoxiong's Arrival in Nanjing

Guangdong Province Proceeding with the Opening of Huangpu Port

Gu Yingfen, Director of the National Government's Civil Affairs Department, had previously suffered from a back tumor and returned to Guangdong for recuperation. He has recently recovered. Chairman Chiang sent a telegram urging him to return to Nanjing. Yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, Mr. Gu, along with Chen Ce, the Administrative Yuan's Political Deputy, and six or seven secretaries, arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong aboard the President Grant. Liu Jiwen, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Zhou Yongneng, the former Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, specially prepared a customs launch to welcome them. At around 9:00 AM, the customs launch docked at the new customs pier. After Mr. Gu and others disembarked, they took a car to the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office on Xinza Road to rest. At 12:00 PM, Mr. Gu, along with Liu Jiwen, Yang Hu, and others, went to the Orthopedic Hospital to visit Xiong Shihui. Mr. Gu took the overnight train to Nanjing at 11:00 PM last night. At 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon, a reporter specially visited Mr. Gu. According to the interview, the removal of the back tumor in Guangdong and the rest in the Sanatorium were quite painful for nearly forty days. The matter of Guangxi is being handled by Ma Xiaojun in Wuzhou, and a peaceful resolution is expected. Huang Shaoxiong had sent a representative, Wu Tingyang, to Guangdong, claiming that Huang would come to Nanjing for a visit, but I did not meet with Huang when I passed through Hong Kong, and I do not know the details. It is now heard that Huang, Li, and others are in Vietnam. The Guangdong Provincial Government has now decided to proceed with the construction of Huangpu Port, which is being carefully planned by the Construction Department. Construction is scheduled to begin next spring, and funding will be allocated from the Boxer Indemnity. As for Zhongshan Port, the Construction Department has detailed the reasons why it cannot be opened to the Provincial Government and requested that it be forwarded to the National Government for approval. Mr. Gu also said that he had visited Zhao Shihui's injuries this afternoon. Xiong's spirits are still good, but his face is terribly thin. The doctor fears that it will damage his mind, so he is still forbidden to talk. It is said that he is expected to recover in about a month. The following is a transcript of the letter from Deng Yanhua, Director of the Guangdong Provincial Construction Department, stating the reasons why Zhongshan Port (i.e., Tangjiawan) cannot be opened.

Submitting a Statement Explaining the Reasons Why Tangjiawan Cannot Be Opened and Requesting the Restoration of Huangpu Port's Opening to Trade. Respectfully Requesting Forwarding to the National Government for Reference and Adoption. The matter of opening Tangjiawan Port has been approved by the National Government. We have also been actively preparing for the opening ceremony. Yanhua originally did not dare to interfere, but because of my position in charge of construction, since the news of the opening of Tangjiawan Port was reported, people in society have repeatedly questioned it, and many have expressed their concerns. Yanhua also considers this to be a century-long plan, so after consulting the Premier's "The International Development of China," and subtly consulting with technical personnel, I believe after repeated studies that Tangjiawan still does not have the possibility of opening a port. Therefore, based on my humble opinion, I briefly state the following: (1) The Premier's "The International Development of China" is an immutable model for all construction in our Party from now on. Upon review, the third plan of "The International Development of China" stipulates 31 commercial ports, namely three world-class ports, four second-class ports, nine research ports, and fifteen fishing ports, but Tangjiawan is not included. The location of each port determined by the Premier must have been carefully considered based on its nature before being determined. If Tangjiawan had the possibility and necessity of opening a port, the Premier, who grew up here, would not have ignored it. Now, abandoning the southern major port (world-class port) stipulated by the Premier, and turning to Tangjiawan, which has not been stipulated, as a major direct trade port, is tantamount to reversing the Premier's original plan in "The International Development of China." (2) As we know, four conditions are the most important for a 良港: One is deep water, two is sheltered waters, three is a large flat area, and four is a large population. If it is an important commercial port, it must also have the possibility of defending itself against enemies. That is, other transportation, food, and water are closely related to the port. However, Tangjiawan, except for the third item, is a big problem. The rest do not meet the requirements of the above conditions. According to the 士河 and 拿馬 canals, they all allow 27-foot draft 船 to come and go. The world's 船 must be at least 27 feet deep. This is clearly evident. However, upon checking the "Map of the Pearl River and Western Tributaries of Guangdong" reprinted by the Japanese Hydrographic Department, published in the first year of Taisho in Japan, and the "Kapsingwuntobccatigris" Venus Gate map published by the British Navy in 1929, the water depth of Tangjiawan is recorded. According to the nautical chart published in 1929, the water depth from A to B is no more than two fathoms (FACHOM), and the water depth from C to D is no more than two fathoms. If a ship of more than 20,000 tons cannot pass through or be berthed (ships of more than 20,000 tons require a depth of at least 27 feet; the remaining deep-water areas are either too far from the port, or blocked by sand deposits, or not suitable for berthing). Furthermore, according to the results of the survey conducted by technicians Cai Baolin, Chen Yunan, and Yang Shaonan sent by my office to Tangjiawan in June and July last year, it is roughly stated that: (1) Near the bay, in addition to sand ridges, rice fields, and the residences of villagers, the rest are high mountains and ridges. (2) The soil in this area is all composed of sand and stone, and its texture is the loosest. Therefore, sand and stone have accumulated in all places near the sea, and the water discharge is not without reason. (3) The wind direction is mostly from the east, and its force is extremely strong. The instruments used were almost blown away by the wind. However, there were no anemometers to test its speed at that time, but it was about 30 miles per hour (referring to the measurements in June and July). There is no sheltered water in the bay, and ships are prone to danger. (4) The highest tidal water accumulation line is 81.69 feet high, and the lowest tidal water accumulation line is 74.29 feet high (referring to the measurement from the assumed elevation). The sea water is quite deep in June and July. In winter, most of the bay surface dries up, and most of the seabed sand and stone can be seen. Therefore, those who pick 　 are everywhere. Even if there is a deep place, the area is also very narrow (obtained from the words of the locals). (5) Most of this bay is sandy bottom and close to the delta outlet sand beach. Therefore, the depth of the sea varies depending on the accumulation and flow of sand. Furthermore, nearby mountains often push sand and stone to the seabed, which is a major problem (see the "Map of the Pearl River and Western Tributaries of Guangdong" by the Japanese Corporation). (6) It rained for three hours on July 13, with a rainfall of up to two inches. (7) Doubt about the water supply. The coastal area of the bay is all saltwater. The villagers rely on a mountain well that is less than a foot full and wells that they have opened themselves as drinking water. Mr. Tang Shaochuan once dug an artificial artesian well last year to supply the drinking water for a village, which is only enough for use. It is still questionable whether it is sufficient for use in prosperous times. The situation shown in the figure and report is already like this. Even if it is forcibly built, it will cost a great deal of engineering, and I am deeply afraid that it will be of no avail. As for the population aspect, there are no more than tens of thousands of people near Tangjiawan. Secondly, in terms of protection, since Tangjiawan is designated as an international direct trade port, it must have a strong defense force to protect it in the event of international war, while Tangjiawan is wide open without any natural defenses, which seems inconsistent with the conditions that a modern commercial port should have. Again, in terms of inland transportation, inland transportation is greatly related to the transportation, collection, and distribution of goods. Therefore, the reason why the Premier designated Guangzhou as a major port in the south is that the existing railways and the planned Southwest Railway system center on Guangzhou (now, the provincial roads of this province also center on Guangzhou). Now, Tangjiawan is located in a remote corner, neither benefiting from the use of existing railway transportation, nor is it possible to change the Premier's original railway plan to accommodate it. In this way, seeking to become a market for the Pacific coast and South China's commercial center is probably not something that can be achieved in a short period of time. Moreover, the only target of this port is Hong Kong. If it does not have sound qualifications itself, it is impossible to talk about seizing the inherent prosperity of others, which is deeply rooted. I remember that when the Premier was alive, I learned from my service that Mr. Chen Yixi, an overseas Chinese merchant from Taishan, repeatedly presented the matter of opening Tonggubu Port, but the Premier did not 　 it because the conditions were not met. It can be seen how cautious the Premier was about opening ports and opening up new ports. Based on the above two points, it can be seen that opening Tangjiawan as a direct trade port may not be permitted by the Premier, nor may it be possible. Furthermore, the Premier promoted the opening of Huangpu Port as a commercial port during his lifetime, as a place for international direct trade. This is a very important part of the work of opening up a major port in the south. However, today, we are proceeding with the opening of Tangjiawan. Does South China need two major direct trade ports at the same time, or will it forever abandon the most likely to prosper Huangpu Port regardless? If so, how should we resolve the issues of receiving overseas Chinese equity, government credibility, and future construction? Yanhua is ignorant and unable to list them all. However, because this matter concerns a century-long plan, and because of the questions and urges of my friends and subordinates, I dare to present my humble opinion and attach a plan of the outer port of Huangpu, a nautical chart of Venus Gate, a map of the Pearl River Western Tributaries of Guangdong, and a land survey map of the vicinity of Tangjia 　, each one copy. Please examine it, and I sincerely request permission to forward it to the National Government for 　 preparation for adoption. Whether it is appropriate is still up to you. 　 Presented to Chairman Chen, Deng Yanhua, Director of the Guangdong Construction Department.

Silver and Money Industry Improvement Collection and Settlement Measures

Money Industry Generally Returns to the Bank of China for Inflow and Outflow

Implemented on January 1st of the Solar Calendar Next Year

The silver and money industry has always collected and settled foreign currency in cash, but there are many risks in transit. Industry leaders have repeatedly considered improvement measures to avoid risks. After a long period of consultation, the consent of the Chinese Merchant Bank Association, the Foreign Merchant Bank Association, and the Money Industry Association was finally obtained a few days ago. Now, the notice of the Money Industry Association is recorded below. I am writing to inform you that the Shanghai Bank Association's letter stated that, after the members of our association proposed to improve the silver dollar collection and settlement methods between Chinese and foreign banks, it was resolved and a letter was sent to the compradors of various foreign banks, stating that in the future, the silver dollar collection and settlement of members of our association with foreign banks will be handled in accordance with the regulations of silver collection and settlement, all remittances will be made to avoid danger and save procedures. After that, a reply was received from the Foreign Merchant Bank Association, also expressing their approval of this, which will be implemented from January 1st of the solar calendar next year. As for drawing horizontal accounts, etc., they must also be sent before 5:00 PM. If they are overdue, they will be regarded as cash settlement. Exchange of banknotes cannot be included in the scope of remittance. According to the above, in addition to notifying the members of our association to investigate and comply, the relevant situation will be sent to your association, and it is hoped that a letter will be sent to the Foreign Merchant Bank Association so that money shops can also handle it in the same way. In this way, the remittance can be unified, and the procedures can be simplified, which is expected to be approved by your association, etc. When it came to our association, it was submitted to the standing committee for public discussion on the 16th of this month. It was decided to handle it in the same way as the Chinese Merchant Bank. After our association sent a letter to the Foreign Merchant Bank Association, a reply was received stating that our association had previously received a letter from the Shanghai Bank Association, stating that in order to reduce risks and facilitate procedures, the silver dollar collection and settlement methods have been improved and will be implemented on a trial basis from January 1st. Our association is very supportive of this measure. However, if the money industry does not join, the silver dollar collection and settlement remittance will still not be unified. Yesterday, a letter was received, knowing that your colleagues are all happy to comply, and we are very happy. However, it is hoped that you will convey to your colleagues that from January 1st, all silver dollar collection and settlement will be returned to the Bank of China for inflow and outflow. However, for those shops that have not entered the park (i.e., those that pick up and beat yuan characters), please also transfer to contact them, and follow the unified method of the large banks. There are still matters that have not been completed, and they will be presented to you at any time, etc. The relevant case will be recorded and notified, etc.

Ministry of Finance Orders the Abolition of the Jiangsu Shatian Official Property Affairs Bureau

Ends by the End of the Year

Handled by the Department of Taxation

The Jiangsu Shatian Official Property Affairs Bureau has now been ordered to be abolished by the Ministry of Finance, and must be terminated by the end of this year. The Ministry has dispatched four committee members to Jiangsu to take over. In the future, the Shatian Official Property Affairs will be under the jurisdiction of the Ministry's Department of Taxation. The people of Jiang and Chang counties had jointly appealed to the provincial government, claiming that the bureau's various tax policies were harming the country and the people, and requested that the regulations be revised and reforms be sought. The provincial government approved it and transferred it to the Ministry of Finance for approval.

The method will be further discussed and decided upon at the National Railway Freight Rate Conference. In addition to ordering various lines to comply, this reply is hereby issued for notification. This concludes the reply.

The National Match Industry Federation submitted six points of consensus reached at the executive and supervisory meeting to the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Executive Yuan. The original text is recorded below: (Submission regarding opinions on the new tax, earnestly requesting approval. As the Ministry of Finance is about to implement the special tax, the association held an executive committee meeting on the 21st of this month to discuss and unanimously resolved to submit opinions to the government. Hereby respectfully submitted as follows: (1) Please do not retroactively collect the special tax on products manufactured before its implementation. All manufactured matches before the implementation of the new tax, regardless of location, should not be retroactively taxed. (Reason) The cost of all manufactured matches before the implementation of the new tax is different from after the new tax. Therefore, they should be handled separately. (2) The burden of raw materials in various regions should remain equal. From January 1st, 20th year, all raw material taxes on matches must be equal across regions. If there are any additional sub-taxes, etc., they should be considered a violation of the Ministry of Finance's explicit order and should be refunded within the special tax. (Reason) Since the special tax is implemented, the burden in various regions should be equal. If there are additional sub-taxes on raw materials, it will not only fail to thoroughly eliminate tariffs, but also destroy equality. Therefore, it must be refunded within the special tax. (3) The special tax should not be an additional or duplicate collection. (1) After the implementation of the new tax, if any taxes, fees, or miscellaneous expenses arise, regardless of their nature, whether central or local, they should be refunded within the special tax. (2) The special tax must be mutually recognized between regions and should not be re-levied due to provincial differences. If such a situation occurs, it should be refunded within the special tax paid in the original region. (3) Special taxes should not be levied on wood, paper, and other match raw materials used for raw materials and materials for collecting special taxes. (Reason) Since the tax has been reformed, efforts should be made to ensure thoroughness, and there should be no duplication of various items. Point 1 is a duplication of taxes on one item, point 2 is a duplication of special taxes in various regions, and point 3 is a duplication of special taxes on raw materials and finished products. (4) The special tax should use the following grading as the standard: 1. Small safety matches with 75 sticks or less (excluding an average of 75 sticks, double-headed broken sticks), or sulfurized phosphorus matches with 100 sticks or less (excluding an average of 100 sticks, double-headed broken sticks), should be classified as lower grade. 2. Medium-box long-stick safety matches with 100 sticks or less (excluding an average of 100 sticks, double-headed broken sticks), should be classified as middle grade. 3. Large-box matches with 125 sticks or less and foreign matches (regardless of the number of sticks and length, as long as it is 125 sticks or less), should be classified as upper grade. 4. For those with an even greater number of sticks, the tax rate should be calculated accordingly. (Reason) Since the types and costs of finished matches are different, special taxes should be levied separately to ensure fairness. (5) Please do not collect any other fees. After the implementation of the new tax, the saltpeter and sulfur transport documents should be immediately abolished. (Reason: Requiring both passports and transport documents for transporting potassium nitrate and sulfur is redundant. After the implementation of the new tax, there is no reason to keep these transport documents and fees. They should be abolished. (6) When implementing the new tax, it is necessary to prevent foreigners from establishing factories in the interior to engage in aggression. 1. Chinese factories (excluding those that do not pay raw material taxes to the Chinese government) should have a portion of the special tax refunded in the name of a reward to differentiate them from foreign-funded factories. 2. The number of factories should be limited to those currently registered with the central government (registration with local government offices is invalid). The reorganization or expansion of old factories should be subject to considerable inspection. If there is foreign investment, the government should prevent it. (Reason) Foreigners have an aggressive intent towards the match industry. Although the new tax simultaneously raises the import tax on foreign matches to 40%, this is not enough to suppress the import of foreign goods. As for factories established by foreigners within China, they pay taxes in the same way as Chinese factories, without any distinction. In the future, foreign merchants will not import from abroad, but will establish factories in China. The disaster may be hundreds or thousands of times greater than today. This reward and the method of restricting the establishment of factories are to prevent foreign aggression. In addition, the match industry in the Northeast has already implemented resistance to foreign merchants' aggression. The special tax system is that every 2,400 boxes, Chinese and foreign, are affixed with a one-yuan-and-fifty-cent stamp tax, but in reality, Chinese factories only pay thirty cents. The Guangdong Province's regulations on the collection of inland consumption tax on matches also have provisions for refunding raw material taxes and other miscellaneous fees. This request is to adopt the precedents of the Northeast and Guangdong. Furthermore, the government has special industrial incentive laws. Now, it is justified to refund a portion of the tax under this name. Moreover, the output of existing Chinese-owned factories already exceeds demand. It is necessary to prevent foreign investment and limit Chinese factories. The sixth item, the incentive and the method of restricting the establishment of factories, is particularly important. If the first to fifth items are affected, the result will be the incomplete elimination of tariffs and the increased burden on merchants. If the two methods in the sixth item cannot be implemented, foreign merchants' aggression will intensify, affecting the future of the entire Chinese match industry. The government's goal of eliminating tariffs and reforming taxes is to relieve the suffering of merchants and rescue industry. It can take overall consideration and make the best judgments. However, as matters concern personal interests, the association's executive committee has resolved to submit opinions, earnestly requesting review, approval, and adoption, for which we will be extremely grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Legislative Yuan by the National Match Industry Federation).

Wine Industry Resumes Work Today

Subsidy Issue for Agencies Finally Resolved Yesterday

The strike in the city's wine industry could have been resolved and work resumed yesterday, but due to the issue of subsidies for agencies' strike losses, normal work could not resume. The situation yesterday is recorded below:

Workers' Congress: At 9:00 AM yesterday, the workers' union convened an emergency meeting of all agencies, chaired by Hu Gu, with formalities. First, the chairman reported on the situation of attending the Chamber of Commerce meeting last night (24th), stating that the Chamber of Commerce had resolved to provide a subsidy of five yuan per person for the agencies' strike losses and to compensate the workers' union based on one yuan per person for the number of agencies. The stamp was also ordered to be abolished by the district bureau. The strike could be considered over. He requested that everyone resume work today. After the report, the agencies felt that giving five yuan was too little and immediately expressed unwillingness to resume work. As a result, it was decided to hold another meeting in the afternoon to resolve the issue.

Emergency Meeting: At 2:00 PM, another emergency meeting of all agencies was convened, chaired by Gu Jiren, with formalities. First, the chairman reported that the morning's attempt to resolve the issue with insufficient compensation failed, which was unfortunate for the union. After discussion by the executive committee, a satisfactory solution was found. If the agencies insisted, it would not be a good sign. If they wanted a slight increase, the Chamber of Commerce's compensation for the union's losses could be transferred to the agencies, totaling six yuan per person. The money would be collected from each shop by the union within three days and distributed to the agencies with a stamp. As for the union's losses, further compensation would be sought from the Chamber of Commerce. Thus, a storm was calmed, and work could resume this morning.

Accepted Conditions: The conditions proposed by both labor and management in this strike have been accepted by the Collection Office, including: (1) Immediately abolish the stamp. This was ordered by the head of the Second District Bureau. (2) Dismiss Zhu Houfu, who incited the strike. Zhu Houfu has now resigned voluntarily. (3) Extend the license application time. This has now been extended from 8:00 AM to 5:00 PM, allowing license applications at any time. (4) The agency should be paid for carrying wine that has been penalized. The office has agreed to subsidize 20 cents per load and 70 cents per basket. (5) The license should be properly affixed, and it should not be forcibly torn or confiscated without reason. This has also been approved. However, the issue of fines must be given a five-part receipt. This has not yet been resolved and will be negotiated after work resumes. The conditions can be considered a victory.

Sea Trials of the "Datong" Warship

A reporter from the Guowen News Agency happened to participate in the sea trials of the Navy's "Datong" warship, which sailed towards Minhang yesterday. Here are the observations for the readers. The ship is 260 feet long, 27 feet wide, 11 feet deep, and has a displacement of 1,000 tons. The specified speed is 21 knots per hour. It is equipped with three large cannons, two anti-aircraft guns, two six-pounder guns, and eight machine guns. During the sea trials, the ship's body was very convenient and without vibration. The speed was as specified. Everything inside the ship was brand new and orderly. The combat equipment, telecommunications, defense supplies were all very agile and continuous.

It is noted that the ship was originally named "Jian'an," built at the Mawei Shipyard. Previously, it had not been repaired for a long time, and officials considered the project too large, almost rendering it useless. Later, Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan made comprehensive plans and ordered the shipyard in May of this year to focus on repairs and renovations, with a deadline of February or March of next year. When Chen concurrently took charge of the shipyard, he was diligent and led by example, greatly inspiring all employees. The ship was completed ahead of schedule, with performance no different from a new ship, but with less than one-tenth of the expenditure. With painstaking efforts and remarkable construction, it is to Chen's credit. The ship is scheduled to hold a flag-raising ceremony on January 1, 20th year, and will be incorporated into the Second Fleet.

Transportation Industry Strives for Exemption from Stamp Duty

Letters to various companies unanimously strive for exemption

The Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway's Hangzhou Transportation Association sent letters to various companies along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway yesterday, stating that on December 2nd of this year, the association, due to the cargo receipt issued by the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Bureau (referred to as the bill of lading), was previously notified by the Transportation Department on August 4th that it was exempt from stamp duty. However, in October, they suddenly received a letter from the city's Stamp Tax Bureau, forcibly ordering their fellow traders to be responsible for purchasing stamps, causing disputes among their fellow traders. A second general meeting of members was held to resolve the issue. After discussion, the members unanimously stated that they should not be responsible for purchasing stamps and vowed to argue reasonably. They presented various reasons (omitted). The reasons stated are very sufficient. All the members have unanimously resolved to prepare a document and argue reasonably. In addition to requesting the Ministry of Finance to withdraw its order and submitting it to the General and Branch Stamp Tax Bureaus, requesting the revocation of the original case of affixing stamps to this bill of lading, a special letter is sent, hoping to investigate and strive for it together.

Petition to Abolish Coal Tax

Respect Government's Prestige

Quickly Relieve Chinese Merchants

The Shanghai Coal Industry Association submitted a document to the National Government Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Industry, requesting the abolition of coal tax to conform to the government's prestige. The coal tax began in July of the 16th year of the Republic and was an unprecedented anomaly. Coal merchants were unfortunate and bore the brunt of it. In the four years since, although it has been reduced twice, more than a hundred coal merchants have been ruined by the coal tax. The implementation of the coal tax is extremely unequal. The same coal is taxed when transported and sold by Chinese merchants, but only registered when transported and sold by foreign merchants, and can be released without obstruction. This method is very painful, and one cannot help but accuse the government of destroying Chinese merchants. The coal tax has been repeatedly petitioned by coal merchants, and the government has used encouraging words, such as the Ministry of Finance's No. 112 reply on October 12th of the 16th year, stating that the coal special tax is a type of commodity tax, which should be abolished immediately after the implementation of tariff reduction and tax increase in accordance with the order of tariff reduction and tax increase and the regulations on the abolition of domestic transit tax. During the active Northern Expedition, there was an urgent need for funds, so please be considerate of the difficult times and maintain the overall situation, and work hard to undertake it. Once the tariff reduction and tax increase are implemented, the special tax will be abolished immediately to take care of both and enrich the people's livelihood. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce's telegram on September 12th of the 17th year slightly stated that the Jiangsu Finance Department reviewed and replied that from September 1st of this year, before the city tariff is implemented, the coal item will still be taxed at the current commodity tax rate of two cents per load in Jiangsu Province, totaling three cents, three cents and six li per ton. The Ministry of Finance's telegram No. 2200 on March 28th of the 18th year slightly indicated that whether the coal tax can be changed depends on whether the tariff reduction has been implemented. The tariff reduction and tax reform are currently in the planning stage, so the coal tax cannot be changed for the time being. Looking at these replies and telegrams, the government clearly indicated that the coal tax would be abolished when the tariff reduction is implemented. The documents are clear as the sun and stars. However, the Ministry of Finance forgot to abolish the coal tax in its telegrams, probably due to being busy with many affairs. In order to respect the government's credibility and quickly relieve the merchants' predicament, a petition has been prepared, and Lu Qisheng, Pan Yisan, and Wang Pingnan have been jointly recommended as representatives. It is humbly requested that the government approve the abolition of the coal tax as soon as possible. The petition is presented.

Page 11

Local News II

New Cooperation Agreement Between Chinese and Foreign Steamships on the Shanghai-Ningbo Route

Effective from New Year's Day

The only Chinese-foreign joint venture route, the Ningbo line, since the Taikoo, China Merchants, Sanbei, Ningshao companies joined forces last year to jointly operate fares, has broken the bad habit of indiscriminate fare reductions in the past. The operating income has increased rather than decreased. The four companies, whose one-year cooperation term has expired, have now continued their joint venture, but with slight revisions to the treaty. After a week of consultations on the new treaty, the four companies have reached a decision and formally signed the agreement yesterday. The details are as follows:

Allocation of Public Funds

The operations of the four companies will continue as originally planned, with 800,000 yuan divided into four shares. Ningshao takes the lead, followed by Sanbei and China Merchants, and lastly Taikoo. The new treaty only increases the control over the allocation of public funds. The original agreement, from January 1, 1931, to December 31, stipulates that the four companies on the Shanghai-Ningbo line shall jointly promote freight agreements. In addition to the allocated amounts, any surplus public funds shall be revised according to Article 4 as follows: The allocation of public funds shall be based on the frequency of each ship, etc., and the allocation method shall be: (1) Xin Jiangtian shall be allocated a freight rate of 10 per trip; (2) Xin Ningshao shall be allocated 11 per trip; (3) Ningyu Xing shall be allocated 10 per trip; (4) Xin Beijing shall be allocated 10 per trip. During the repair period of each ship, each company may send a ship of equal tonnage to replace it. In case of accidents, such as engine damage, requiring suspension of navigation for more than one month, the company may send another ship, but the allocation rate shall be determined separately by the four companies.

Revision of Discounts

According to the current Shanghai-Ningbo freight table, the original price is calculated at an 85% discount. It has now been decided that from March 1, 1931 of the Republic of China, this 85% discount will be cancelled, and the full original price will be charged. By that time (i.e., before March 1), the four companies will separately sign a freight agreement to implement this.

Addition of Armed Guards

Due to the unrest at sea, merchant ships in the waters off Zhejiang often suffer from pirate attacks. The ships of the four companies on the Shanghai-Ningbo line do not yet have armed guards. This issue has been raised for discussion at this meeting, and the four companies have unanimously agreed to stipulate in the new agreement that (B) each company may deploy armed guards on the Shanghai-Ningbo route, and the expenses may be moderately offset by slightly increasing passenger fares. This matter is already being discussed by the four companies for implementation.

Transshipment Commissions

The 85% discount for goods shipped from Shanghai has been cancelled. The weight discount for goods transshipped from Ningbo to Shanghai is: (1) 15% for Hong Kong and Guangdong; (2) 20% for various ports in the North. The commission is calculated at 95% for ordinary passengers. In addition, each company may designate three customs brokers to receive a special discount of 10% (calculated from the gross amount) every year on January 1 and July 1. The Ningbo passenger discount is also calculated and paid in accordance with the first and seventh months of the lunar calendar, and no advance payments are allowed. The cotton commission is deducted at 15% for cash discount and 10% for period discount, both calculated on the net amount. This new contract is divided into Chinese and English versions (each company holds one copy, effective from New Year's Day).

Theft of Tobacco Leaves at China Merchants Bureau

Stolen Tobacco Leaves All Recovered

South Warehouse Staff Under Custody

General Manager Li Makes Major Rectifications

Hopes for Clearing Up Long-Standing Abuses

The theft of tobacco leaves from warehouses is common everywhere. The abuses in this regard are most difficult to detect and eliminate. Since taking over the China Merchants Bureau, General Manager Li Zhonggong has been renovating the warehouses to establish great trust with customers and eliminate abuses among staff. Recently, a large shipment of tobacco leaves from Xuchang was transported to Shanghai and unloaded into Warehouse No. 7 in the South Warehouse, totaling more than 6,000 pieces. The value of this tobacco is very high. After being stored in the warehouse, it was discovered that several pounds were missing from each piece of tobacco leaves. General Manager Li received the information and immediately ordered a secret investigation by the Inspection Department, which unexpectedly found the stolen goods in the warehouse.

Original Stolen Goods Found

The Inspection Department of the South Warehouse assisted the staff of the Dingji tobacco company in searching Warehouse No. 7. As expected, more than 30 pieces of tobacco leaves were found in the miscellaneous grains stored in the warehouse, worth about 2,000 yuan. It is believed that the thieves were unable to transport the stolen goods out in time and had no choice but to mix them with the miscellaneous grains, intending to sell them out later when the opportunity arose.

Clearing and Unloading Goods

General Manager Li is handling this matter very seriously, as only in this way can he gain the trust of customers and eliminate long-standing abuses. He has ordered all tobacco merchants to unload and clear all 6,000 pieces of tobacco leaves to determine the amount of stolen goods. He has also ordered the Warehouse Department to inspect other goods to find out if there are any other stolen items. Therefore, Warehouse No. 7 has been very busy unloading goods in recent days, and the situation will be thoroughly clarified soon.

Warehouse Staff Under Custody

The thieves who stole the tobacco have not yet been found. Although the stolen goods have been recovered, no one has confessed to the theft. However, warehouse staff member Weng Youshan has a specific job responsibility and cannot shirk responsibility. It is still difficult to determine whether he is guilty of self-theft under his supervision. Yesterday, General Manager Li ordered the Inspection Department of the South Warehouse to place Weng under custody for further investigation after the warehouse is cleared. After this incident occurred, customers have expressed sympathy and trust for Li's serious efforts to eliminate abuses and protect merchants' goods.

Two Young Girls Kidnapped in Yu Dong Port Outside Songkou

Cui Changlin's Family Suffers an Unexpected Calamity

First Robbed, Then Two Daughters Kidnapped

Around 11 PM the night before last, two pirate ships with more than 20 pirates armed with guns suddenly landed at Yu Dong Port outside Wusongkou and stormed into the home of Cui Changlin to rob. Before leaving, they kidnapped Cui's eldest daughter, Qiaolin (19 years old), and second daughter, Qiaozhen (13 years old). During the journey, Qiaozhen tried to escape but was shot and wounded by the pirates, falling by the roadside. The pirates then carried Qiaolin onto the pirate ship, set sail, and fled, claiming that a ransom must be prepared within a week.

Fire in Gaoqiao, Pudong Burns Two to Death

Husband and Wife Intend to Become Mandarin Ducks of Shared Fate

Poor Firefighting Leads to Fire Spreading to Two Homes

Chen Qiuting, a 54-year-old farmer with the address of No. 75, Dong, San Guantang area, Gaoqiao, Pudong, and his wife, Chen Ling, 46 years old, were boiling water in the kitchen to wash their feet before going to bed the night before last. After going to sleep, the fire was not completely extinguished, causing the embers to fall on the firewood, and a raging fire quickly erupted, turning into a prairie fire. The Chens, who had been working hard during the day, were sleeping soundly at night and did not wake up. By the time the fire burned them and the smoke filled the house, there was no way out. The couple died together in the fire, becoming mandarin ducks of shared fate. The firefighting equipment in the area was poor, so the fire spread to the homes of Fan Wangsheng at No. 74 and Chen Xiaohong at No. 76. Despite strenuous efforts to put out the fire, most of the houses were burned down, but the fire did not spread to other neighbors. The bodies of Chen Qiuting and his wife were not pulled out until yesterday. Gao Linquan, the local security officer of the 17th District, reported the matter to the local court for inspection, while Chen Xiaoting, the deceased's brother, petitioned the court to waive the inspection.

A Bowl of Rice Leads to Death

Old Mother Speaks with Emotion

Son Intends to Sacrifice Himself

Zhou Jiyun, a native of Funing who lives in a bungalow at No. 67, Longhua Road, Gaochang Temple, makes a living by pulling a rickshaw. His son, Zhou Buqing, 22 years old this year, follows in his father's footsteps and continues his father's business. However, the family has many mouths to feed, and the daily cost of food is quite high, making life extremely difficult. At dinner the day before yesterday, Zhou Buqing had a large appetite and ate an extra bowl of rice. His mother, Yang, said to him, "There are still people who haven't eaten yet, eat less." After hearing these words, Zhou Buqing felt a great shock and silently went to bed. Yesterday, when the sun was three poles high, he had not yet gotten up. His father pushed open the door and saw that he had hanged himself on the bed and died. His body was cold and stiff. The whole family cried. The police reported the matter to the Second District Police Station, which ordered Ji Anguo, the local security officer of the 14th District, to report to the local court. The family requested a waiver of the inspection, but it was not approved. After Inspector Yang arrived to inspect the body, he ordered it to be collected for burial.

Vacancy for Foreign Engineer in the Dredging Bureau Filled by a Chinese

The Dredging Bureau decided after negotiations between negotiator Jin Qian and Chief Engineer Hai Qian and Tax Officer Mei that foreign engineers who leave the Dredging Bureau would not be replaced and that Chinese engineers would be used instead. Therefore, when Hart, a British supervisor at the Zhanghuabang factory of the Bureau, was distributing salaries on a mud dredging ship on the Huangpu River, he was killed by a gunshot. At the time, Director Song advocated that Chinese be used to fill the vacancy and advertised for applications. However, because the qualifications of the Chinese applicants were insufficient, a French Russian named Que Bolin (the person who was assassinated) was temporarily hired. The vacancy he left has now been temporarily filled by Zhu Hua, the deputy construction engineer sent by the Bureau. It is recently rumored that the person to succeed him as the factory supervisor of the Bureau has not yet been selected, and Director Song Ziliang still advocates that Chinese engineers should be hired in accordance with the resolution to comply with the original plan. However, this matter must await a meeting before a decision can be made.

Jiangjiatang in Minhang Robbed

Fifty to Sixty Robbers

Arrived with Torches and Weapons

Jiangjiatang Village, about seven or eight li from Minhang Town, Shanghai County, is a remote place where Jiang Honggen, Jiang Xiaoan, Jiang Shulou, Jiang Jialiang, Jiang Jiajing, etc., live together. Around 1 AM the night before last, fifty to sixty robbers suddenly arrived with torches and weapons and stormed into the village, breaking down doors and entering to loot at will. The entire village was robbed, and the details of the stolen goods have not yet been determined. Jiang Jialiang, one of the victims, resisted the robbers at the time, resulting in head and waist injuries. After hearing the alarm, Director Pan of the First Branch of the County Police and Commander Wu of the First District Security Corps immediately led the entire team of police and militia to rush to the scene to apprehend the robbers, but they had already gone far away. They immediately reported the situation to the County Public Security Bureau for instructions. Yesterday morning, Director Yan Jian personally traveled to Minhang by car, accompanied by Director Pan and Commander Wu, to visit the scene of the incident, investigate the situation in detail, and inquire about the robbery. He then returned to the city. Before leaving, he instructed Director Pan and others to tighten the investigation and ensure that the case is solved and the criminals are punished within days to deter bandits.

Robbery of a Farmhouse

Entire Family Pulled Out of Sleep

All Were Bound to Chairs

Only Untied the Following Morning

Around 11 PM the night before last, more than ten robbers speaking with a northern accent and with painted faces suddenly arrived at the home of Wang Nianchun, a resident of Wangjiazhai, about six li northwest of Wusong, and broke open the gate and rushed in. At that time, Wang had gone to Shanghai for business and had not returned. His wife, Zou, and children were all fast asleep. They were dragged out of bed by the robbers, tied to chairs with ropes, and their mouths were tightly stuffed with cotton. The robbers then began to rob. Hearing dogs barking in the distance, the robbers were afraid of being exposed, so they took the stolen goods and fled to the west with a whoop. Wang's family saw the robbers go far away and wanted to untie the ropes and report to the neighboring village, but the ropes were tied to the back of the chairs, making it impossible to do so. Their mouths were stuffed with cotton, making it impossible to shout. It was not until dawn that a neighbor passed by their house, saw the door open, and heard no sound. Upon entering, they discovered that the Wang family had been robbed and untied Wang's wife and children from the chairs. When Wang returned home around 10 AM yesterday, he inspected the stolen clothes, jewelry, silver dollars, etc., and the losses amounted to more than 500 yuan. He has already reported the matter to the police station for investigation.

Mrs. Hou Chen Sues for Severance of Mother-Son and Mother-Daughter-in-Law Relationship

Dispute over Whether Adopted or Biological Son

Investigation of Evidence Attempted to Resolve the Matter

Mrs. Hou Chen, a widow residing at No. 364, Yongtai Lane, Zhaofeng Road, has a son named Guisheng, who was originally working as a runner in a roulette gambling house at No. 181, Fuxu Road. He witnessed the casino granting prizes of sixty or seventy yuan, enough to support his mother, sister, and family. However, his mother was also addicted to gambling, particularly flower games, day and night, with little success, leading to mounting debts. Lin Sheng, unable to dissuade her, took his wife, Ms. Xu, and moved out, ceasing to provide for her needs. Mrs. Hou Chen then caused disturbances at the gambling house, leading the owner to fire Guisheng. Guisheng's resentment towards his mother deepened, and he incited his wife, Ms. Xu, to gather aggressive women to provoke her. Therefore, Mrs. Hou Chen hired a lawyer to sue in the Special District Local Court, seeking permission to sever the mother-son and mother-daughter-in-law relationship with Guisheng and Ms. Xu. According to her petition, after marrying Hou Caisheng, she only had a daughter named Xinggen. Lacking a son, she adopted Guisheng and financed his education from a young age, hoping he could become independent. However, Guisheng used studying as a pretext to associate with ruffians. After Caisheng's death fifteen years ago, he became even more reckless. In March of the previous year, to marry Xu Xuliang's daughter, Chengbao, hoping for his reform, the defendants colluded and frequently started arguments, demanding money. On July 11th of this year, incited by her father, she gathered many female thugs to assault her, only to be dispersed by neighbors. Later, they invited people to her house and forcibly took away her clothes and belongings. Such disrespect and intolerance are unbearable. She specifically requests a judgment to sever the mother-son and mother-daughter-in-law relationship. After being sued, Guisheng hired lawyer Hong Shihao to file a defense, denying being the plaintiff's adopted son, claiming to be Caisheng's biological son. When Caisheng was critically ill, he cut his arm to make soup, hoping to cure his father's illness, with the remaining scar still visible. If he were not his biological father, who would do this? He started working outside at the age of sixteen, with half of his monthly salary taken by his mother. His sister and wife's needlework income was also mostly handed over to the plaintiff, so his monthly income was no less than one hundred yuan. The reason for the mounting debts is that his mother set up both a "Swallow's Nest" (a gambling den) and played flower games. Having such a mother, what could he do? Recently, his job was lost due to his mother's disturbance. He relies on his wife's work to make a living and has no extra money to support his mother. Now, she wants to break the relationship, intending to recruit another son-in-law, disrupting the bloodline and damaging property. It is difficult to remain silent and requests the rejection of her lawsuit. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Yi opened the court for a hearing. Both parties held their own views on whether he was an adopted or biological son. Besides oral statements, there was no written evidence. Judge Yang studied the case for a long time, stating that to conduct a trial according to law, evidence must be investigated. He instructed both parties to retreat and attempt reconciliation. If reconciliation fails, a further hearing will be scheduled.

Mei Lanfang Agrees to Perform for Henan Disaster Relief

Subsequent Performances Scheduled in About Twenty Days

Henan Province has suffered from continuous years of disaster. This time, it has been further ravaged by war. Now, with the cold weather and the year-end approaching, disaster victims are exposed and starving, with countless deaths due to cold and hunger. Zhang Fang, the former Director of Civil Affairs of the Henan Provincial Government, came to Shanghai to report on the disaster situation in Henan and to consult with Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Committee, as well as Wang Yiting, Wang Xiaolai, Yuan Ludeng, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, and others, requesting them to persuade Mei Lanfang, Wang Fengqing, Tan Fuying, Jiang Miaoxiang, Yao Yufu, and other famous Shanghai opera stars to perform for disaster relief to save the victims. On the evening of the previous day at 7 PM, Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, and Li Zushen hosted a public banquet for Mei, Wang, Tan, Jiang, and Yao at the Dahua Hotel, and invited Tu Xiaolai, Yuan Ludeng, Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuesheng, Xie Hengchuang, Zhao Jinqing, Yu Zhihao, as well as Fan Zhengbo from the Municipal Party Headquarters and Li Zizhong, a representative from Henan, to attend. Xu Shiying first reported on the severity of the disaster in Henan and stated that Dr. Mei had agreed to perform for disaster relief. He offered a modest banquet as a toast. Then, Fan Zhengbo (from Henan) and Li Zizhong gave a detailed report on the Henan disaster, almost breaking down in tears. They also thanked Dr. Mei on behalf of the Henan disaster victims. Dr. Mei then rose to speak, saying that his visit to Shanghai was short and he might not be able to stay long. However, after listening to Chairman Xu and Fan and Li's reports, the disaster in Henan was severe, and he should do his utmost to fulfill his duty. However, the originally scheduled performance date was still more than twenty days away. He should proceed with subsequent performances after this period, which he would be very willing to do. Yuan Ludeng continued the speech, saying that Dr. Mei was a world-renowned figure. The current disaster situation in Henan was so severe. Dr. Mei's appearance on stage to help relief was known to the world, who would certainly say that the people of our country have the virtue of helping their compatriots. As for himself, he was also a member and should follow gentlemen like Shi Xiaojun, do his best to help, and would never decline. Li Zushen also gave a speech and raised a glass to Dr. Mei. Toasts were exchanged, and everyone enjoyed themselves until 10 PM, when they dispersed.

The Municipal Social Bureau previously received a report from the Municipal Coal Industry Association stating that recently, someone claiming to be Wu Dan, a councilor from the Fifth Division Headquarters, claimed to have obtained the names and addresses of the leaders of various industry associations from the Municipal Social Bureau with permission from the Social Bureau to solicit donations for the Henan Province Military Disaster Relief Committee. The Bureau stated that hooligans were using charity as a pretext to solicit donations for personal gain in the city, and had already issued a notice prohibiting this. All legitimate charitable acts must have the donation booklet submitted to the Bureau for official stamping in advance to be valid. Regarding whether there was a councilor Wu Dan in the Fifth Division, a letter was received from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters stating that the Fifth Division had no such person. This Wu Dan was impersonating a public official, engaging in fraud and swindling outside, which was particularly hateful. A letter had been sent to the Public Security Bureau to instruct them to strictly investigate and arrest him for prosecution.

Compensation of 500 Yuan Each to the Families of the Deceased

The Ningbo Jinbaoli lighter was violently sunk by the Yongmao, a fishing vessel of the Nanshi Yongsheng Fishing Company, at Zhanghuabang, Wusong, around 5:00 PM on the 13th of this month, resulting in the loss of the vessel and its cargo, and the drowning of three crew members. Pu Zhao River to Undergo Pipe Laying

The Pu Zhao River in Western Shanghai, from Xie Bridge to Xin Bridge, has long been planned by the Public Works Bureau to have a main ditch buried since the Health Bureau filled it with garbage, so that the sewage from the nearby roads can be discharged without obstruction. However, due to the vast expenses, it has not yet been started, causing flooding during rainy days, much to the suffering of the residents. Recently, it has been learned that the Municipal Government, recognizing the urgency of this project, has allocated special funds and set a date to begin construction. It is also heard that this project will be temporarily divided into two phases due to financial constraints. The current construction, from Xie Bridge to Jumen Road, is the first phase. After the entire project is completed, the sewage from the nearby roads should no longer be blocked.

Attention for Those Who Use Coal Briquettes for Heating

The Qi Family Died from Poisoning

Their Son is Well After Treatment

Wang Yujin, a native of Ningbo, currently residing at No. 229, Xiangyu Lane, Yuanfang Road, Hongkou, is over forty years old and works as a coppersmith at the Electric Company. His wife, Qi, is thirty years old and has only one son, who is still in his swaddling clothes. Yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, Wang went out to work. Because of the recent cold weather, Qi placed a coal briquette stove in the room and held her beloved son to warm him. Unexpectedly, she suffocated and died from coal poisoning. It was not until nearly 11:30 AM that a neighbor pushed open the door and saw it. There was no way to revive her, but the child still had a breath of life. He hurriedly called her husband, Wang Yujin, back home, reported to the police station, and ordered the police to take the child's body and send it to Tongren Hospital. The child was treated by a doctor and was found to be well. The body was transferred to the autopsy institute for autopsy.

Iron Sheet Breaks the Bridge of the Nose

Iron Sheet from the Muzzle of a Shotgun Ricochets

Wang Yaokun's Life is in Great Danger

Wang Yaokun, a native of Changzhou, is thirty-one years old and works as a coppersmith at the British American Tobacco Company in Pudong, number 60. Yesterday was Christmas, and the factory was closed as usual. In the afternoon, at a little after 1:00 PM, Wang took a shotgun to the nearby garden to shoot birds. Because the gun had not been used for a long time, the mechanism was inevitably damaged. Unexpectedly, when a bullet was fired, an iron sheet about 2 inches long and 2.5 inches wide on the muzzle suddenly jumped up and ricocheted back, hitting Wang's nose bridge. The nose bridge bone was broken, and blood gushed out, rendering him unconscious. He was seen by villagers, taken by car to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Wang's injury is said to be very serious, and there is concern for his life.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Distributes Outlines for Business Tax and Consumption Tax

All Industries Should Pay Attention After the Abolition of Likin

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations yesterday, stating, "Greetings. On the 22nd of this month, we received a letter from the Municipal Joint Association of Domestically Manufactured Goods Factories stating that the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Committee resolved to abolish likin on New Year's Day next year and plans to implement three types of taxes: factory tax, business tax, and special consumption tax to compensate for the loss. The outlines for the factory tax and business tax, and the implementation outline for the special consumption tax, have been formulated by the government, and we assume that your association has records of the resolutions of the Five Provinces' Likin Abolition Conference. A representative has been sent to request that you copy one of each for reference. We have found that factory tax is a type of consumption tax and is already included in the implementation outline for the special consumption tax. We believe that these provisions are necessary for reference by all industries. Therefore, we have reprinted multiple copies of the full text based on previous reports, including the outlines for the provincial collection of business tax methods, the implementation outline for the special consumption tax, and the resolutions of the Five Provinces' Likin Abolition Conference, and have sent them to various trade associations for reference. Please acknowledge receipt."

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter Seafarer

Son (Returning from a long journey. He has been a guest in a foreign land for seven or eight years. He arrives at the door. He asks a newly hired servant.) Is the Madam at home?

Servant (Looking the son up and down) Who are you? Did our Madam ask you to come?

Son Don't worry about it. I want to see her. She is waiting for me.

Servant Ah? She is waiting for you? (Acting surprised)

Son (Smiling) Yes. Even before I was born, she was waiting for me. Because she is my mother.

Mother (Asking her nine-year-old daughter) Child, do you miss your father?

Daughter Of course, I miss him. Father has been away for three years.

Mother Today, I'm going to write him a letter. Would you like to send him a kiss in my letter?

Daughter Mother, would it be okay to send it tomorrow? Because I just ate onions today.

Middle-aged woman (Arriving at a shop, speaking to a shop assistant.) Do you have many kinds of handkerchiefs here?

Shop assistant Very, very many. What kind of handkerchief does the Madam want?

Middle-aged woman Take out a few more for me to look at.

Shop assistant Our goods are all good quality. (Taking out box after box for her to see. She looks at dozens of boxes.)

Middle-aged woman (Very happily pointing to a box) Yes, yes. This is the one. How much does this box cost?

Shop assistant Madam, it only costs four yuan a box. How many boxes do you want to buy?

Middle-aged woman I don't want to buy any. It's just that someone happened to give me a box like this, and I want to ask about the price.

Special Habits of Several Friends Pine Shadow

People's preferences are like their faces; each has its own characteristics, whether sweet, sour, bitter, or spicy. For example, Gu Hongming's fondness for small feet, Tan Yankai's love of pig trotters, Zhang Taiyan's habit of playing with bronze Buddhas when writing, and Wu Tingfang's love of humorous conversation are all well-known. Friends also have their own particular preferences, and I will record a few to provide material for after-dinner conversation.

Yu Youren likes to wear cloth socks. The beautiful beard of Yu Youren, a prominent figure in the Party and the country, is no less impressive than that of Guan Yu. Many people recognize him. His life also has its own special characteristics. Regardless of age (young, middle-aged, or old), season (spring, summer, autumn, or winter), or location (north, south, center, or foreign), for decades, he has only worn old-fashioned white bamboo cloth socks. He has never worn the popular double-strand cotton and silk stockings. The big-bearded Mr. Yu is indeed a loyal customer of Hong Mao Chang.

Tu Luyi, the "Bathhouse Inspector." Wang, a close associate of Yu, once served as the Secretary-General of the Secretariat of the Central Party Headquarters. He is currently the head of the Chinese Literature Department at Anhui University. He is a romantic and talented individual. Last year, while living in Shanghai, he was bored and, in his spare time, diligently bathed. He tried all the large and small bathhouses in the Public Concession, French Concession, North and South cities, and Pudong, and is very familiar with the layout, prices, and services of each bathhouse. Friends call him the "Bathhouse Inspector Commissioner."

Jiang Tianduo Collects Cigarette Holders. Jiang Tianduo, a lawyer who previously served as the Director-General of the National Water Conservancy Bureau and the Vice Minister of Agriculture and Commerce, is a lifelong enthusiast of smoking cigarettes, especially collecting cigarette holders. Over the years, he has acquired no less than several hundred types. The prices range from over 500 yuan for an expensive one to only a few cents for a cheap one. They come in all shapes and sizes and are truly unique. When arranged and displayed, they resemble a cigarette holder exhibition.

Chu Wenjuan Resists Ear Piercing. Female new literary writer Chu Wenjuan... Chess World Joke by Shen Shouruo

Our country's chess skills have unfortunately fallen behind, often allowing the Japanese to take the lead. This, although a small matter, is enough to glimpse the subtle signs of national strength and weakness. Therefore, people are also competing and trying their best to improve. The competitive spirit is flourishing, cultivating local talent and creating national glory. This is also a good sign.

While we were contemplating the layout of the chess pieces, we heard a joke that made us laugh heartily. The storyteller said that upstairs in a certain chess club, some people were playing Go, while downstairs, two people were playing Chinese chess. Occasionally, they argued and even resorted to violence, causing a great commotion for some time. Later, the two of them understood each other, stopped fighting, and said that the people playing Go upstairs were quiet and not as rude as them, which made them feel ashamed. They decided to go upstairs to watch. When they got upstairs, they saw one person grabbing the other's throat, locked in a stalemate. They then realized that they were also arguing, but silently. There have always been jokes and strange tales, but rarely chess jokes, so I wrote it down.

...publishes works in various publications without adding the word "Ms." to her name. If the editor adds it, she sends a letter requesting that they not do so again next time. She is now almost thirty years old and has never worn earrings. Since childhood, she has refused to pierce her ears, so she has no earrings to wear. Her revolutionary nature is innate, so her works also avoid describing sensual or erotic content.

Li Jianfeng Collects Talismans. Li Jianfeng, a epigrapher, has spent over forty years collecting talismans and incantations from various regions. He has also searched extensively in remote areas such as Tibet and Outer Mongolia. He currently has over 9,270 types, which are mounted in ten large volumes. Each page is labeled separately, indicating the source and application. It is said that he spent over a hundred yuan on a few pages to acquire them. If compiled and photographed, it would become a grand compendium of talismans, an indispensable material for researchers of society.

Preparations for the Great Cleaning Wang Meiyu

The Bureau has issued a proclamation that the 25th day of the 12th month of the national calendar will be the day for the great cleaning. It is said that residents everywhere dare not disobey. There are many interesting stories during this preparation period. Please record them to enrich this talk. A long-time friend who lives near Suzhou and Hangzhou came to Shanghai yesterday to talk over drinks. He mentioned the implementation of the national calendar and said that the three dynasties of Zi, Chou, and Yin built it successively, which is not surprising. Then he told the recent stories of the Li and Zhou families in his hometown. The Li family is relatively well-off. A female servant named Chen has been employed for more than five years. She is extremely cautious and willing. Her home is not far away, but no one has ever come to visit. The master doubles his efforts to take care of her. All the belongings are entrusted to her management. Recently, the master said that he would comply with the order to carry out a major cleaning. She was very unhappy. She said, "Why bother with this trivial matter? Besides, we live in a remote rural area. Who will actually see it?" The master laughed at her stubbornness. Then Chen suddenly claimed to be sick and asked to leave, presenting her luggage for inspection one by one. She left early the next morning. After she left, a neighbor told the master that Chen had too many items with her. After the master inspected carefully, he found that some clothing, ornaments, cups, and chopsticks were missing. It turned out that although no one came to Chen's home, she would go home three or four days every one or two months to celebrate. This time, the cleaning order was issued outside of her normal return period, so she was forced to flee. This is one story. At the same time, an even more interesting thing happened in the neighboring village of Zhou. Zhou's household has two wives, the first wife Huang and the second wife Shen. Both are from small families. They are distinguished as older and younger based on the order in which they entered the door, but neither is his original wife. Huang is more straightforward but lacks harmony. Her interactions with Shen are sometimes talkative and laughing, sometimes conflicted and quarreling, but without any preconceptions. Shen, on the other hand, never offends. Huang is happy, she is happy; Huang is angry, she is not angry. Many people praise her. She is also more beautiful than Huang. Zhou knows a little about writing and can read newspapers. He also has the ambition to present himself to society and find a small position. He usually pays attention to the policies of the National Government. Yesterday, he told his two wives that they should enjoy themselves as much as possible during the upcoming New Year and that they should comply with the order to carry out a major cleaning on the 25th day of the 12th month. Huang, being impatient, immediately started tidying up the scattered items in the room. Zhou sat by and watched. Shen suddenly came in and laughed, "You're sweating profusely! Why are you in such a hurry?" She helped Huang tidy up. Huang refused, but Shen didn't listen and said, "There are three people in the room. I certainly won't be a thief in a trunk!" Then she pushed Huang to sit for a while. As she was pushing, something fell from Huang's sleeve to the ground. Zhou picked it up and his expression changed. He asked, "Who is she? Who is she? And why are you taking this side-by-side photo with her?" Huang said, "This is just a little sister dressing up and taking pictures. Who did you think it was?" Shen laughed again and said, "Where is that person? Quickly call her over and it will be clear!" Zhou still shouted loudly to clean out this thief. This is another story. I asked if he had witnessed both events. The long-time friend said, "I heard one and saw the other."

Travel Notes on Southeast Asia (112)

Burmese women are also very willing to marry Chinese men, as they want to enjoy comfort and avoid their own hard work. They especially welcome those in the Chinese education sector. Chinese men often marry a Burmese woman locally and use her language skills and business acumen to cooperate and become wealthy. This often happens, and it is also the most convenient path to wealth. There are already many people of mixed Chinese and Burmese ancestry. Many Chinese live in villages and engage in commerce and industry throughout the country. There is almost no place where they are not present. The depth of this relationship should not be underestimated.

Traveling in various ports in Southeast Asia presents a common difficulty. The confusion of languages and names is already a problem, but the street names posted on the street walls by Westerners are too small, and sometimes they are blurry and unclear, making it difficult to find them. Finding street names is the most important task for the municipality, and everyone needs to do it. How can the characters be small and blurry? I remember that the citizens of Nanjing once had an exemplary action that was worthy of being the best in the world. That is, every main street has a specially erected archway over ten feet high, with the street name written in large characters. This point is very commendable. Without comparison, one cannot know the strengths and weaknesses of oneself and others. In various ports in Southeast Asia, the ditches and sewers are not covered, which is very harmful to hygiene.

Burma has the name "Golden Burma" (GOLDBURUINA), allowing people to share its riches. The British take over its full authority. The Indians, the rich become big merchants, the intelligent become officials. Indians are often used as officials, second only to the British. The lower class are the so-called "Kala people" who pull rickshaws, shave heads, and sell coffee and tea. The Japanese, both men and women, often practice medicine here. Everyone eats in Burma and returns fully loaded. Burma gets poorer day by day, but because of abundant rainfall, rice production, timber, silver mines, and gems are produced in limitless quantities. Burmese people are still content and happy. The Great Golden Pagoda of Burma is indeed a great benefactor.

Warmth in the Heart (3) (4) (3) Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Sixteen: Cui Xiu Earnestly Asks the Teacher for Advice, Heroic Women Feast in the Brothel, Talking Boldly About War

Time passes even faster in confusion. In the blink of an eye, it is already March or April. The spring god has created many light green and rich green clothes and put them on many tall and short branches. They are also decorated with countless red, purple, yellow, and white ornaments, dressing up a spring earth in a magnificent and unparalleled manner. Everywhere, men and women are frolicking in the spring. That prosperous and famous Shanghai does not have any place for outings. Only in March, people go to Longhua to see peach blossoms, run horse-drawn carriages, and after the emergence of cars, they go there to take a car ride. In fact, it can be considered meaningless to the extreme. Therefore, people who have lived in Shanghai for a long time, if they want to change the air, still go to Suzhou and Hangzhou to walk around. There are many places to travel. Shanghai has no scenic spots and no historical sites, only full of foreign stench. However, the horse races in spring and autumn every year are still closed and the market is closed. Many people run to watch the horse races. The brothels in Shanghai take advantage of this name to ask guests to eat a few more tables of wine. Crows are all black in the world, and the madams are all the same. Seeing the guests, they all ask them to eat wine and play cards. Zuo Shichen often walks around in Luyi's place. Even if they don't ask him, he feels embarrassed not to fulfill a little obligation. At that time, he agreed on a date, and Zuo Shichen went to write an invitation ticket to summon many friends. Naturally, Ling Zhixiang, Lin Fanzi, and Long Ziyun were indispensable. Among the new friends, there were also Wei Ziyi and Sun Qilei. Originally, Wei Ziyi and Zuo Shichen were classmates. Although Wei Ziyi was from Biling, he often lived in Suzhou. After Mr. Xu passed the imperial examination, he taught in his home, specializing in teaching the two brothers. At that time, Zuo Shichen was engaged in the study of writing test papers and followed that old Mr. Xu. Every month, he had to write nine articles. Mr. Xu urged him very strictly. If he wrote one less, he would be uncomfortable and would ask you why you wrote one less this month. Originally, his writing schedule was three, six, and nine, the third, sixth, and ninth of each month, the thirteenth, sixteenth, and nineteenth, the twenty-third, twenty-sixth, and twenty-ninth. While Mr. Xu was teaching students in his home, he would also invite you to his home for an interview on the writing schedule. He was willing to invite you to eat a meal so that you could not escape from writing articles. But if you wrote nine articles every month, he would also correct nine articles every month and never leave them there unattended. Zuo Shichen was his favorite student, so later, when he taught at the Wei family, he often taught him to send his articles to him to see. At that time, Wei Ziyi and Wei Ziqian were still young, only eleven or twelve years old and seven or eight years old. All day long, they would not stop in their chairs. When they saw Senior Brother Zuo coming, they were very happy. Because the teacher and Senior Brother Zuo were talking about articles, they could stop reading their books.
